## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: chemical reaction kinetics
**Analysis**: This task models the rate of change of concentration dA/dt as a function of concentration A and time t, which is the fundamental problem of determining reaction rate laws. The rate typically depends on powers of concentration, and time-dependence may arise from photochemical, catalytic, or coupled reaction effects.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Zero-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 (constant rate, independent of concentration)
- First-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A (rate proportional to concentration, radioactive decay, unimolecular reactions)
- Second-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**2 (bimolecular reactions with single species)
- nth-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 (general power-law rate law)
- Mixed-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A) (second-order with stoichiometric constraint, A+B->products where B=c1-A)
- Michaelis-Menten type: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A) (enzyme-catalyzed or saturation kinetics)
- Autocatalytic reaction: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A)**c2 (autocatalysis with finite substrate)
- Reversible first-order: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 (forward and reverse first-order reactions)
- Inhibition kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A**2) (substrate inhibition)
- Competitive product inhibition: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A + c2 * A**2) (complex enzyme kinetics)
- Time-dependent rate: dA_dt = c0 * A * exp(c1 * t) (time-varying rate constant, e.g., temperature ramp)
- Parallel reactions: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 * A**2 (simultaneous first and second order pathways)
- Langmuir-Hinshelwood: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A)**2 (surface-catalyzed bimolecular reaction)
- Fractional order with offset: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 + c2 (fractional order with constant source/sink)
- Cooperative kinetics (Hill-type): dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 / (c2 + A**c1) (cooperative binding/reaction)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Pure concentration power-law dependence (dA/dt ~ A^n) indicates an elementary reaction of order n; integer orders suggest simple molecularity
- Rational functions of A (numerator/denominator polynomials in A) indicate enzyme or surface catalysis with adsorption/saturation
- A product term A*(c-A) suggests a bimolecular reaction between a reactant and a species whose concentration is linearly related to A (conservation law)
- Explicit time dependence beyond what A(t) provides suggests externally driven conditions (temperature ramp, photolysis, or time-varying catalyst activity)
- Negative dA/dt with positive A indicates consumption (reactant); sign of the rate constant encodes whether A is produced or consumed
- Square in the denominator (c+A)^2 indicates bimolecular surface reactions following Langmuir-Hinshelwood mechanism
- Logarithmic corrections ln(A) may appear in diffusion-limited or fractal kinetics scenarios
- Sum of multiple power-law terms in A suggests parallel competing reaction pathways with different orders
- A Hill-type sigmoidal dependence on A (A^n/(K+A^n)) indicates cooperative or allosteric effects in biochemical kinetics

## Analysis

The Ground Truth (GT) numerical expression is:
$$f(t, A) = 0.08820105614498638 \cdot A \cdot \log(0.4381050266935539 \cdot t + 1) - 0.9112380846295999 \cdot A \cdot \exp(-0.08901020540483869 \cdot t)$$

This has two terms:
1. An exponential decay term: $A \cdot (\text{const}) \cdot \exp((\text{negative const}) \cdot t)$
2. A logarithmic term: $A \cdot (\text{const}) \cdot \log((\text{const}) \cdot t + 1)$

**Candidate 5**: `A*c0*exp(c1*t) + A*c2*t**c3 + A*c4*log(c5*t + 1) + c6`

This candidate can match the GT by setting:
- $c0 = -0.9112380846295999$ (coefficient of the exponential term)
- $c1 = -0.08901020540483869$ (exponential decay rate)
- $c2 = 0$ (eliminates the $A \cdot t^{c3}$ term)
- $c3$ = any value (doesn't matter since $c2 = 0$)
- $c4 = 0.08820105614498638$ (coefficient of the log term)
- $c5 = 0.4381050266935539$ (inside the logarithm)
- $c6 = 0$ (no constant offset)

With these assignments:
$$A \cdot (-0.9112) \cdot \exp(-0.0890 \cdot t) + 0 + A \cdot 0.0882 \cdot \log(0.4381 \cdot t + 1) + 0$$

This exactly matches the GT expression.

**Candidate 5 is a match.**

For a candidate to match, it must be able to reproduce exactly these two basis functions. Since `log` and `exp` and polynomials are linearly independent, candidates without a `log` term cannot match (unless they somehow construct one, which is impossible with the available building blocks).
